This is Bob Brown Left In mucius prompta maiorum mel. In this lesson you will move through a number of information screens which will teach you about [Lesson Title].

You will also be presented with scenario pages, where a situation will be described involving a number of fictitious characters. You will be asked questions which will test your understanding of [Lesson Title].

These questions are not scored and your response is not recorded. Use the feedback provided to consolidate what you have learned during this lesson.

Learning Objectives
This lesson should take about 20 minutes.
You will learn about the Use and Disclosure Principle that sets out the rules for how you can use and disclose personal information.
At the end of the module you should have a good understanding of:
  • the ways that organisations can use and disclose personal information in general
  • the special rules that apply to direct marketing and to the exchange of information between related companies
To get started, please click on thenext button below.

Light globe at top of mountain
The Use and Disclosure Principle sets out the rules for how you can use and disclose personal information.
When does it apply?
The principle applies when you use or disclose personal information that was collected by your organisation after 21 December 2001 (whether that information is collected directly from an individual or from a third party).
What are the rules for using and disclosing personal information?
You can always use and disclose personal information for the main purpose that it was collected for. The main purpose is called the "primary purpose" in the National Privacy Principles (NPPs).
The primary purpose of collection can be determined from the context in which the information was provided. For example, if a new customer supplies personal information to your organisation for the purpose of buying a product or service, the sale of that product or service by your organisation would be the primary purpose of collection.
You can only use or disclose personal information for another purpose in certain situations.

Man with clipboard
You cannot use or disclose personal information for purposes other than the primary purpose except in any of the following situations. Other purposes are called "secondary purposes" in the NPPs.
  • If the other purpose is related (in the case of sensitive information, directly related) to the primary purpose of collection, and individuals would reasonably expect their personal information to be used or disclosed for the other purpose.
  • If individuals have consented to the use or disclosure of their personal information for the other purpose
  • If the use or disclosure is required or authorised by law
  • If it is necessary to prevent a serious threat to an individual's life, health or safety
  • If it is necessary to prevent a serious threat to public health or public safety
  • In investigations of unlawful activity (such as fraud) as long as the disclosure is necessary to the investigation
  • If it is reasonably necessary to help official enforcement agencies
 Click here to view a definition of sensitive information Sensitive information means any information relating to an individual's:
  • health
  • racial or ethnic origin
  • political opinions
  • membership of a political association, professional or trade association or trade union
  • religious beliefs or affiliations
  • philosophical beliefs
  • sexual preferences or practices
  • criminal record
 There are certain other situations where the use or disclosure of information for secondary purposes is permitted. These are specified in the Use and Disclosure Principle. true Using Personal Information for Direct Marketing Computer
You can use (but not disclose to third parties) personal information for direct marketing if:
  • direct marketing is the primary purpose of collecting the personal information.
  • direct marketing is related to the primary purpose of collection and individuals would reasonably expect their information to be used for direct marketing
You can also use personal information for direct marketing if ALL of the following apply:
  • the information being used is NOT sensitive information
  • it is not practical to seek consent before using the information for direct marketing
  • the individual has not previously told you that they do not want to receive direct marketing material from you
  • you display a notice letting individuals "opt-out" of future direct marketing
  • you do not charge individuals for choosing to opt-out
  • you set out your organisation's address and phone number, or its fax or email address if the direct marketing was by fax or email
You cannot use sensitive information for direct marketing purposes without specifically obtaining an individual's consent.

Globe Click here to view a definition of related companies Two companies are related if:
  • one company is a holding company of the other company;
  • one company is a subsidiary of the other; or
  • they are sister companies, that is, they share the same parent company.
If you have any questions about whether your organisation is related to another company, you should contact the legal department.
 Your organisation can disclose personal information (but not sensitive information) to a related company if you told the individuals that you would do so when you collected the information or as soon as practicable after collection. The related company that collects the personal information does not need to make the disclosures ordinarily required under the notice requirements of the Collection Principle. Click here to view the Notice Requirements of the Collection Principle Notice Requirements of Collection Principle
When you collect information from individuals, you must take reasonable steps to make them aware of all of the following information:
  • the name of your organisation and how to contact it
  • that individuals are able to access the information held about them
  • the purposes of collection
  • the organisations or types of organisations that your organisation usually gives this information to
  • if the information is required by law
  • the main consequences, if any, for the individual if they do not provide you with the information
A related company that collects information in this way can only use and disclose the information for purposes that it was originally collected for.
For example, if you collect information for the purpose of improving customer service you can disclose that information to a related company but the related company can only use the information for improving customer service.

Joe
Joe is a member of the customer service team for ACME Superannuation Limited. Joe has access to the customer inquiries database that contains name and address details of prospective customers who have telephoned ACME to inquire about superannuation.
Joe thinks this valuable information could be used for many other purposes. He would like to analyse the information and compare profiles of people who inquire about ACME's superannuation plans with those who actually buy thesuperannuation plans. ACME could then build up profiles of particular customers and determine the success rate of different sales and customer service techniques. These sales and service techniques (and not the customer information) could, in turn, be used to establish a customer service training business as an adjunct to ACME's core business activities.
 Is this a use or a disclosure issue? Use
Yes.
Even though ACME will not be "disclosing" the information to a third party, it will still be "using" the information internally, so the Use and Disclosure Principle applies.
 Disclosure
No.
The information is not being "disclosed" to any third party. However, the information is being "used" internally, so the Use and Disclosure Principle applies.

Joe Joe runs his idea past Jeremy, ACME's legal counsel. Will Jeremy tell Joe that using customer inquiry information in this way: is okay because the information is only being used internally by ACME
No.
The Use and Disclosure Principle applies to internal use of personal information in the same way it applies to "external" use of personal information.
Prospective customers have provided their details for the primary purpose of receiving information about ACME's superannuation. The use of the information to establish a customer service training business is not a purpose related to the primary purpose of collection and individuals would not reasonably expect their personal information to be used for this purpose.
If ACME wants to use its customers' information in this manner, it must ask for their consent.
 is okay because it is related to the primary purpose of collection and the individual would reasonably expect ACME to use it in this way
No.
Prospective customers have provided their details for the primary purpose of receiving information about ACME's superannuation. The use of the information to establish a customer service training business is not a purpose related to the primary purpose of collection and individuals would not reasonably expect their personal information to be used for this purpose.
 is not allowed because it is not related to the primary purpose of collection
Yes.
If ACME wants to use its customers' information in this manner, it must ask for their consent.

Clarisse Clarisse is the privacy officer of St Martins Bank. Clarisse has had several requests from government agencies and other third parties for the personal details of clients of the bank. On occasions, she has felt uncomfortable when she has released information. She asks Stephen, the bank's legal counsel, for his advice on how she should handle the following situations. What should Stephen's advice be - can St Martins Bank disclose personal information in these situations? An Assistant Police Commissioner phones up and asks for details of a client who is under investigation for money laundering
Yes.
But this information should not be given over the telephone. The Police should be asked to put their request in writing. St Martins Bank can disclose information to assist enforcement agencies, if Clarisse and Stephen are satisfied that the information requested is 'reasonably necessary'. If they obtain evidence that a warrant has been issued St Martins Bank would not need to take any further precautions before disclosing the requested information.
 The Australian Tax Office requests quarterly returns on interest paid to clients
No.
The Tax Office does not have power to require regular returns of this sort. Clarisse should insist on a formal notice citing the relevant authority under tax law.
 A solicitor requests details about one of St Martins Bank's client that he is representing in a property dispute
No.
St Martins Bank should obtain written authorisation from the client to provide this information to the solicitor.
 Another bank (not part of the St Martins Bank group) wants details of a mutual client whom they suspect of fraud
Yes.
The Use and Disclosure Principle allows for the disclosure of information for the investigation of unlawful activity, as long as the disclosure is necessary to the investigation.
 A solicitor asks for financial information about one of St Martins Bank's clients she expects to call as a witness in a complex trial
No.
This request should be refused. Information should only be disclosed in this situation if the solicitor has a subpoena.

/hjHkUS6LYP7kfM4Zc2MOT0rSf8AjmWv/GJf1ZilmeaZWv8Afr8jk8X1NeT6WAfmD/vYnzOZWPmWnJ9LC4/tN88yS40Vlz9hfljFjNn/AOS//Hb1D/mFH/JxMhl5MQ9Lbqc0xdiFGTIFsCg+QbAsPQYlKlJ0+/KykKL/AMciWQeDX3+90/8Art+vOqh9IdBk+ooc5JqZXp/+6/8AUH6swMvV3mLkP6qPPfMdvW4VLOPL3/HLt/8AU/42bNLqf7wto5Jge+YiVjYQqk/TJJf/2Q== Justin
Justin is the sales manager for mobiles phones at Fones4U. ByteIT provides Fones4U's IT services. Justin is not very impressed with the quality of ByteIT's services. Justin knows that Computers4U, a related company to Fones4U, generally uses individuals who are independent contractors for its IT services. Justin asks his counterpart at Computers4U to send him a copy of the Computers4U contractor database for the purpose of acquiring IT services. Justin mentions this idea to Louise, the marketing manager of Fones4U in passing.
Although Louise thinks ByteIT is doing a good job, she thinks that the contractor database contains a lot of information that would be valuable for marketing purposes, including salary information. Louise thinks the IT contractors would be a great sample market for Fones4U's new 3G mobile phone products.
 How do you think Fone4U's legal counsel would view this? Louise has come up with a winner - because the contractors' information was collected by Computers4U, a related company, Fones4U can use the information and does not have to comply with the notice requirements of the Collection Principle
No. Louise hasn't come up with a winner.
Louise is correct in thinking that Fones4U does not need to notify the contractors of all the matters listed in the Collection Principle when Fones4U collects personal information from its related company, Computers 4U provided that Computers 4U has disclosed it will disclose the information about contractors to its related companies. However, Fones4U can only use that information for the purposes for which it was collected by Computers 4U.
In this case, Computers4U collected the information for the primary purpose of managing and acquiring IT services from contractors. Fones4U could use this information for the same purpose (as envisaged by Justin) or another related purpose which the contractors would reasonably expect.
The marketing activities which Louise proposed are not a related purpose.
 Louise needs to go back to the drawing board
Yes. Louise does need to go back to the drawing board.
Louise is correct in thinking that Fones4U does not need to notify the contractors of all the matters listed in the Collection Principle when Fones4U collects personal information from its related company, Computers 4U provided that Computers 4U has disclosed it will disclose the information about contractors to its related companies. However, Fones4U can only use that information for the purposes for which it was collected by Computers 4U.
In this case, Computers4U collected the information for the purpose of managing and acquiring IT services from contractors. Fones4U could use this information for the same purpose (as envisaged by Justin) or another related purpose which the contractors would reasonably expect.
The marketing activities which Louise proposed are not a related purpose.
